Plant Biol. 30, 134–142 (2016)." href="/articles/s41588-018-0110-3#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d17619e2160">59</a></sup>, such that the ancestral genome is a ‘median’ or ‘intermediate’ genome consisting of a clean reference-gene order common to the extant species investigated.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec16">Biochemical analyses of scent composition in roses</h3><p>Volatile compounds were extracted with hexane from petals and stamens of roses of the different genotypes, mainly as previously described<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 28" title="Magnard, J. L. et al. Biosynthesis of monoterpene scent compounds in roses. Science 349, 81–83 (2015)." href="/articles/s41588-018-0110-3#ref-CR28" id="ref-link-section-d17619e2172">28</a></sup> (Supplementary Note <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41588-018-0110-3#MOESM1">9</a>). Camphor was used as an internal standard to estimate compound quantities. Hexane sample fractions were analyzed with a gas chromatograph coupled to an electron ionization mass spectrometer detector (Agilent 6850) operated under an ion-source temperature of 230 °C, a trap emission current of 35 µA and a 70-eV ionization energy. All experiments were performed at least twice. Chromatographs were analyzed in Agilent Data Analysis software, and the volatile substances were identified by screening the WILEY 275, NIST 08 and CNRS libraries to compare MS spectra. The Kovats retention index of each substance was calculated with data of the injection of a homologous set of <i>n</i>-alkane (C<sub>8</sub>–C<sub>20</sub>) according to the Kovats formula<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 60" title="Adams, R. P. Identification of Essential Oil Components By Gas Chromatography/Mass Spectrometry.. 4th edn. (Allured Publishing Corporation, Carol Stream, IL, USA, 2007)." href="/articles/s41588-018-0110-3#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d17619e2187">60</a></sup>. Mass-spectra similarities together with Kovats-retention-index values were then used for compound identification. Concentrations were calculated through comparison of the camphor area as the internal standard.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec17">ChIP–seq assays</h3><p>Petals were collected from <i>R. chinensis</i> ‘Old Blush’ and fixed in 1% (vol/vol) formaldehyde. ChIP assays were performed with anti-H3K9ac (Millipore, 07-352) or anti-H3K27me3 (Millipore, 07-449) according to a procedure adapted from Veluchamy et al.<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 61" title="Veluchamy, A. et al. LHP1 regulates H3K27me3 spreading and shapes the three-dimensional conformation of the arabidopsis genome. PLoS One 11, e0158936 (2016)." href="/articles/s41588-018-0110-3#ref-CR61" id="ref-link-section-d17619e2202">61</a></sup>. Library quality was assessed with an Agilent 2100 Bioanalyzer (Agilent), and the libraries were subjected to high-throughput sequencing on an Illumina NextSeq 500 instrument. After trimming, reads were aligned to the <i>R. chinensis</i> genome in bowtie2 (ref. <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 62" title="Langmead, B. &amp; Salzberg, S. L. Fast gapped-read alignment with Bowtie 2. Nat. Methods 9, 357–359 (2012)." href="/articles/s41588-018-0110-3#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d17619e2209">62</a></sup>) with a maximum mismatch of 1 bp and unique mapping reported. To determine the target regions of H3K9ac ChIP–seq, model-based analysis of ChIP–seq (MACS2)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 63" title="Zhang, Y. et al. Model-based analysis of ChIP-Seq (MACS). Genome Biol. 9, R137 (2008)." href="/articles/s41588-018-0110-3#ref-CR63" id="ref-link-section-d17619e2213">63</a></sup> was used. Detection of H3K27me3-modified regions was performed with SICER<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 64" title="Zang, C. et al. A clustering approach for identification of enriched domains from histone modification ChIP-Seq data. Bioinformatics 25, 1952–1958 (2009)." href="/articles/s41588-018-0110-3#ref-CR64" id="ref-link-section-d17619e2218">64</a></sup>. HOMER<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 65" title="Heinz, S. et al. Simple combinations of lineage-determining transcription factors prime cis-regulatory elements required for macrophage and B cell identities. Mol. Cell 38, 576–589 (2010)." href="/articles/s41588-018-0110-3#ref-CR65" id="ref-link-section-d17619e2222">65</a></sup> was used to annotate H3K9ac peaks with nearby genes if peaks were located in windows −2 kb to +1 kb around the gene TSS. For H3K27me3 peaks, bedtools intersect<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 56" title="Quinlan, A. R. &amp; Hall, I. M. BEDTools: a flexible suite of utilities for comparing genomic features. Bioinformatics 26, 841–842 (2010)." href="/articles/s41588-018-0110-3#ref-CR56" id="ref-link-section-d17619e2226">56</a></sup> was used, and only genes that overlapped with this specific modification were kept. Clustering of H3K9ac and H3K27me3 peaks was performed with SeqMINER<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 66" title="Ye, T. et al. seqMINER: an integrated ChIP-seq data interpretation platform. Nucleic Acids Res. 39, e35 (2011)." href="/articles/s41588-018-0110-3#ref-CR66" id="ref-link-section-d17619e2230">66</a></sup>. Rstudio, Circos<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 67" title="Krzywinski, M. et al. Circos: an information aesthetic for comparative genomics. Genome Res. 19, 1639–1645 (2009)." href="/articles/s41588-018-0110-3#ref-CR67" id="ref-link-section-d17619e2234">67</a></sup> and NGSplot<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 68" title="Shen, L., Shao, N., Liu, X. &amp; Nestler, E. ngs.plot: Quick mining and visualization of next-generation sequencing data by integrating genomic databases. BMC Genomics 15, 284 (2014)." href="/articles/s41588-018-0110-3#ref-CR68" id="ref-link-section-d17619e2238">68</a></sup> were used for graphic representation of histone modifications.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec18">RNA preparation and qPCR analyses</h3><p>Total RNA and small RNAs were prepared from petals at three developmental stages: noncolored petals early during development (closed bud; stage 1); petals at the onset of anthocyanin synthesis (closed bud; stage 2); and fully colored petals with maximum anthocyanin content (bud opening; stage 3). Total RNA was prepared as previously described<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 69" title="Dubois, A. et al. Tinkering with the C-function: a molecular frame for the selection of double flowers in cultivated roses. PLoS One 5, e9288 (2010)." href="/articles/s41588-018-0110-3#ref-CR69" id="ref-link-section-d17619e2250">69</a></sup>. One microgram of RNA was used in reverse-transcription assays, and qPCR was performed as previously described<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 70" title="Dubois, A. et al. Genomic approach to study floral development genes in Rosa sp. PLoS One 6, e28455 (2011)." href="/articles/s41588-018-0110-3#ref-CR70" id="ref-link-section-d17619e2254">70</a></sup> with gene-specific primers (Supplementary Note <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41588-018-0110-3#MOESM1">10</a> and Supplementary Tables <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41588-018-0110-3#MOESM1">8</a> and <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41588-018-0110-3#MOESM1">9</a>). Small RNAs were extracted with a Macherey-Nagel NucleoSpin miRNA kit. Contaminating DNA was removed with an Ambion DNA-free kit. RNA concentrations were measured with a NanoDrop ND-1000 Micro-Volume spectrophotometer (NanoDrop Technologies) before and after DNase treatment. Small-RNA quantification was performed with stem-loop RT–PCR as previously described<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 71" title="Marcial-Quino, J. et al. Stem-loop RT-qPCR as an efficient tool for the detection and quantification of small RNAs in Giardia lamblia. Genes (Basel) 7, E131 (2016)." href="/articles/s41588-018-0110-3#ref-CR71" id="ref-link-section-d17619e2268">71</a></sup>. Reverse transcription was performed with a RevertAid kit (Thermo Fisher Scientific). Primers specific to 5.8S rRNA or stem-loop RT-primer for miR156 (Supplementary Note <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41588-018-0110-3#MOESM1">10</a> and Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41588-018-0110-3#MOESM1">8</a>) were used. 5.8S rRNA and miR156 expression were quantified with a QuantStudio 6 Flex Real-Time PCR 384 instrument (Applied Biosystems) with a Fast SYBR Green Master Mix kit (Roche Diagnostic) and specific primers (Supplementary Note <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41588-018-0110-3#MOESM1">10</a>). Data were collected for three independent biological replicates.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec19">Code availability</h3><p>Source code (in C) and linux binaries of the til-r software are available at <a href="http://lipm-bioinfo.toulouse.inra.fr/download/til-r/">http://lipm-bioinfo.toulouse.inra.fr/download/til-r/</a> under the GPL license.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec20">Reporting Summary</h3><p>Further information on experimental design is available in the Nature Research <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41588-018-0110-3#MOESM2">Reporting Summary</a>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec21">Data availability</h3><p>The <i>R. chinensis</i> ‘Old Blush’ homozygous genome has been deposited in DDBJ/ENA/GenBank under accession number <a href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/nuccore/PDCK00000000">PDCK00000000</a>. PacBio raw data have been deposited in the Sequence Read Archive (SRA) under study accession number <a href="https://trace.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/Traces/sra/?study=SRP119907">SRP119907</a>. The <i>R. chinensis</i> ‘Old Blush’ heterozygous genome has been deposited under BioProject accession number <a href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/bioproject/PRJEB24406">PRJEB24406</a>.</p><p>Resequencing sequence reads have been deposited in the SRA under study accession number <a href="https://trace.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/Traces/sra/sra.cgi?study=SRP119986">SRP119986</a>.</p><p>Hi-C data have been deposited under SRA accession numbers <a href="https://trace.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/Traces/sra/?run=SRR6189546">SRR6189546</a> and <a href="https://trace.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/Traces/sra/?run=SRR6189547">SRR6189547</a>, and ChIP–seq data have been deposited under SRA accession numbers <a href="https://trace.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/Traces/sra/?run=SRR6167310">SRR6167310</a>, <a href="https://trace.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/Traces/sra/?run=SRR6167311">SRR6167311</a>, <a href="https://trace.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/Traces/sra/?run=SRR6167312">SRR6167312</a> and <a href="https://trace.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/Traces/sra/?run=SRR6167313">SRR6167313</a> and under Gene Expression Omnibus accession number <a href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/geo/query/acc.cgi?acc=GSE109433">GSE109433</a>.</p></div></div></section>

P. Vergne and P. Villand produced the rose homozygous line. C.L.-R. and M. Bendahmane performed PacBio sequencing data production. J. Szécsi performed flow cytometry experiments. P.H. provided <i>Rosa</i> material. M. Verdenaud, D.L., M. Benhamed and M.P. performed epigenome analysis. O.R., X.F., S.-H.Y., A.D., M.L.B. and M. Bendahmane performed DNA/RNA sample collection and data production. J.J., M. Verdenaud, M.L., L.F. and O.R. performed RNA-seq and analyses of gene expression. M. Benhamed, M. Verdenaud, C.L., A. Boualem and A. Bendahmane performed chromosome conformation capture Hi-C. M. Benhamed and M. Verdenaud integrated the assembly and genetic map to build pseudochromosomes. J.G. developed bioinformatics tools and assembled the PacBio homozygous genome. M. Benhamed and M. Verdenaud validated the assembly with Hi-C and genetic data. P.W. and A. Lemainque performed Illumina sequencing. A. Boualem and A. Bendahmane provided resequencing sequencing data. A.C., J.-M.A., A.M., K.L. and P.W. assembled the heterozygous rose Illumina sequencing data. N.C., H.Q. and J.J. conducted repetitive DNA analysis. J.G., N.C. and J.J. annotated protein-coding genes, TEs and miRNAs. J.G., H.B., J.J. and L.C. performed bioinformatics analyses. S.C. built the <i>Rosa</i> web portal. J. Salse and C.P. conducted paleoevolution analyses. J.J. and O.R. conducted miRNA analyses. A. Larrieu, T.V. and J.J. performed integrated analyses on auxin genes. S.M., J.-C.C. and S.B. performed gas chromatography–mass spectrometry analyses of scent compounds. S.M., J.-C.C., S.B., O.R. and J.J. performed integrated analyses on scent genes. O.R., L.P., F.P., L.F. and M. Verdenaud performed integrated analyses on flowering genes. M. Vandenbussche performed integrated analyses on MADS transcription-factor genes. O.R., L.F., J.J., L.P., J. Szécsi. and V.B. performed integrated analyses on color genes. M.L.-B., B.G. and Y.L. performed integrated analyses on meiosis genes. H.B., O.R. J.G., J.J. and F.P. performed diversity analysis. M. Bendahmane and J.G. coordinated the rose genome consortium. M. Bendahmane, O.R., H.B. and J.G. wrote the manuscript.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="corresponding-author">Corresponding author</h3><p id="corresponding-author-list">Correspondence to
                <a id="corresp-c1" rel="nofollow" href="/articles/s41588-018-0110-3/email/correspondent/c1/new">Mohammed Bendahmane</a>.</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="ethics" data-title="Ethics declarations"><div class="c-article-section" id="ethics-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="ethics">Ethics declarations</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="ethics-content">
              
                <h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="FPar1">Competing interests</h3>
